# Check if CPUID exists
checkcpuid:
	pushf # Dump CPU flags into the stack
  100193:	9c                   	pushf
	popl %eax # Pop the flags into the EAX register
  100194:	58                   	pop    %rax
	movl %eax, %ecx # Storing a copy of these flags so we don't end up modifying the CPU flags
  100195:	89 c1                	mov    %eax,%ecx

  100197:	35 00 00 20 00       	xor    $0x200000,%eax
	pushl %eax # Push the modified flags into the stack
  10019c:	50                   	push   %rax
	popf # Put the modified flags into the CPU flags register
  10019d:	9d                   	popf
	pushf # Lets check if the bit was flipped and restore the flags
  10019e:	9c                   	pushf
	popl %eax
  10019f:	58                   	pop    %rax
	pushl %ecx # ECX contains our original copy of our flags
  1001a0:	51                   	push   %rcx
	popf # Restore the flags
  1001a1:	9d                   	popf

uint8_t inb(uint16_t port) {
    uint8_t value;
    asm volatile (
  100b30:	89 fa                	mov    %edi,%edx
  100b32:	ec                   	in     (%dx),%al

        : "=a"(value)
        : "Nd"(port)
    );
    return value;
}

0000000000100b40 <io_wait>:

void io_wait() {
    // This is a common technique to create a small delay.
    // Writing to an unused port (0x80) which is historically used for delays
    asm volatile (
  100b40:	31 c0                	xor    %eax,%eax
  100b42:	e6 80                	out    %al,$0x80
        "outb %%al, $0x80"
        :
        : "a"(0)
    );
}
